   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Exploration of the Moon
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4095" data-file-width="4074" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg/220px-Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg/330px-Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg/440px-Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lunar_module_AS12-51-7507.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_12" title="Apollo 12">
          Apollo 12
         </a>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunar_module" title="Lunar module">
          lunar module
         </a>
         <i>
          Intrepid
         </i>
         prepares to descend towards the surface of the Moon.
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
           NASA
          </a>
          photo.
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The physical
       <b>
        exploration of the Moon
       </b>
       began when
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_2" title="Luna 2">
        Luna 2
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Space_probe" title="Space probe">
        space probe
       </a>
       launched by the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union
       </a>
       , made an impact on the surface of the
       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
        Moon
       </a>
       on September 14, 1959. Prior to that the only available means of exploration had been observation from Earth. The invention of the
       <a href="/wiki/Optical_telescope" title="Optical telescope">
        optical telescope
       </a>
       brought about the first leap in the quality of lunar observations.
       <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">
        Galileo Galilei
       </a>
       is generally credited as the first person to use a telescope for astronomical purposes; having made his own telescope in 1609, the mountains and craters on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunar_surface" title="Lunar surface">
        lunar surface
       </a>
       were among his first observations using it.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
        NASA
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">
        Apollo program
       </a>
       was the first, and to date only, mission to
       <a href="/wiki/Moon_landing" title="Moon landing">
        successfully land humans on the Moon
       </a>
       . The first landing took place in 1969, when astronauts placed scientific instruments and returned
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunar_sample" title="Lunar sample">
        lunar samples
       </a>
       to Earth.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">
        Early history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploration_of_the_Moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Selenography" title="Selenography">
        Selenography
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_theory" title="Lunar theory">
        Lunar theory
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Micrographia_Schem_38.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1683" data-file-width="1187" height="312" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Micrographia_Schem_38.jpg/220px-Micrographia_Schem_38.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Micrographia_Schem_38.jpg/330px-Micrographia_Schem_38.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Micrographia_Schem_38.jpg/440px-Micrographia_Schem_38.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Micrographia_Schem_38.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A study of the Moon from
         <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hooke" title="Robert Hooke">
          Robert Hooke's
         </a>
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Micrographia" title="Micrographia">
           Micrographia
          </a>
         </i>
         , 1665
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">
        ancient Greek
       </a>
       philosopher
       <a href="/wiki/Anaxagoras" title="Anaxagoras">
        Anaxagoras
       </a>
       (d. 428 BC) reasoned that the Sun and Moon were both giant spherical rocks, and that the latter reflected the light of the former. His non-religious view of the heavens was one cause for his imprisonment and eventual exile.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In his little book
       <i>
        On the Face in the Moon's Orb
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Plutarch" title="Plutarch">
        Plutarch
       </a>
       suggested that the Moon had deep recesses in which the light of the Sun did not reach and that the spots are nothing but the shadows of rivers or deep chasms. He also entertained the possibility that the Moon was inhabited.
       <a href="/wiki/Aristarchus_of_Samos" title="Aristarchus of Samos">
        Aristarchus
       </a>
       went a step further and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aristarchus_On_the_Sizes_and_Distances" title="Aristarchus On the Sizes and Distances">
        computed the distance
       </a>
       from Earth, together with its size, obtaining a value of 20 times the
       <a href="/wiki/Earth_radius" title="Earth radius">
        Earth radius
       </a>
       for the distance (the real value is 60; the Earth radius was roughly known since
       <a href="/wiki/Eratosthenes" title="Eratosthenes">
        Eratosthenes
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Although the Chinese of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Han_Dynasty" title="Han Dynasty">
        Han Dynasty
       </a>
       (202 BC–202 AD) believed the Moon to be energy equated to
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Qi" title="Qi">
         qi
        </a>
       </i>
       , their 'radiating influence' theory recognized that the light of the Moon was merely a reflection of the Sun (mentioned by Anaxagoras above).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Needham_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Needham-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was supported by mainstream thinkers such as
       <a href="/wiki/Jing_Fang" title="Jing Fang">
        Jing Fang
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Needham_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Needham-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       who noted the sphericity of the Moon.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Needham_2-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Needham-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Shen_Kuo" title="Shen Kuo">
        Shen Kuo
       </a>
       (1031–1095) of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Song_Dynasty" title="Song Dynasty">
        Song Dynasty
       </a>
       (960–1279) created an allegory equating the waxing and waning of the Moon to a round ball of reflective silver that, when doused with white powder and viewed from the side, would appear to be a crescent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Needham_2-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Needham-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       By 499 AD, the Indian astronomer
       <a href="/wiki/Aryabhata" title="Aryabhata">
        Aryabhata
       </a>
       mentioned in his
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Aryabhatiya" title="Aryabhatiya">
         Aryabhatiya
        </a>
       </i>
       that reflected sunlight is the cause behind the shining of the Moon.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hayashi08Aryabhata_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hayashi08Aryabhata-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_W_Draper-The_first_Moon_Photograph_1840.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="360" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/John_W_Draper-The_first_Moon_Photograph_1840.jpg/200px-John_W_Draper-The_first_Moon_Photograph_1840.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/John_W_Draper-The_first_Moon_Photograph_1840.jpg/300px-John_W_Draper-The_first_Moon_Photograph_1840.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/34/John_W_Draper-The_first_Moon_Photograph_1840.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_W_Draper-The_first_Moon_Photograph_1840.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The earliest surviving
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daguerrotype" title="Daguerrotype">
          daguerrotype
         </a>
         of the Moon by John W. Draper (1840)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luna1865_Lewis_Morris_Rutherfurd.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="870" data-file-width="721" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Luna1865_Lewis_Morris_Rutherfurd.jpg/200px-Luna1865_Lewis_Morris_Rutherfurd.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Luna1865_Lewis_Morris_Rutherfurd.jpg/300px-Luna1865_Lewis_Morris_Rutherfurd.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Luna1865_Lewis_Morris_Rutherfurd.jpg/400px-Luna1865_Lewis_Morris_Rutherfurd.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Luna1865_Lewis_Morris_Rutherfurd.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Photo of the Moon made by
         <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Morris_Rutherfurd" title="Lewis Morris Rutherfurd">
          Lewis Rutherfurd
         </a>
         in 1865
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Habash_al-Hasib_al-Marwazi" title="Habash al-Hasib al-Marwazi">
        Habash al-Hasib al-Marwazi
       </a>
       , a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astronomy_in_medieval_Islam" title="Astronomy in medieval Islam">
        Persian astronomer
       </a>
       , conducted various observations at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astronomy_in_medieval_Islam#Observatories" title="Astronomy in medieval Islam">
        Al-Shammisiyyah observatory
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">
        Baghdad
       </a>
       between 825 and 835 AD.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Langermann_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Langermann-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Using these observations, he estimated the Moon's diameter as 3,037 km (equivalent to 1,519 km radius) and its distance from the Earth as 346,345 km (215,209 mi), which come close to the currently accepted values.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Langermann_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Langermann-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the 11th century, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physics_in_medieval_Islam" title="Physics in medieval Islam">
        Islamic physicist
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alhazen" title="Alhazen">
        Alhazen
       </a>
       , investigated
       <a href="/wiki/Moonlight" title="Moonlight">
        moonlight
       </a>
       , which he proved through
       <a href="/wiki/Experiment" title="Experiment">
        experimentation
       </a>
       originates from
       <a href="/wiki/Sunlight" title="Sunlight">
        sunlight
       </a>
       and correctly concluded that it "emits light from those portions of its surface which the sun's light strikes."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Toomer-463-4_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Toomer-463-4-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       By the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </a>
       , before the invention of the telescope, an increasing number of people began to recognise the Moon as a sphere, though many believed that it was "perfectly smooth".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1609,
       <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">
        Galileo Galilei
       </a>
       drew one of the first telescopic drawings of the Moon in his book
       <i>
        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Sidereus_Nuncius" title="Sidereus Nuncius">
           Sidereus Nuncius
          </a>
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       and noted that it was not smooth but had mountains and craters. Later in the 17th century,
       <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Riccioli" title="Giovanni Battista Riccioli">
        Giovanni Battista Riccioli
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Maria_Grimaldi" title="Francesco Maria Grimaldi">
        Francesco Maria Grimaldi
       </a>
       drew a map of the Moon and gave many craters the names they still have today. On maps, the dark parts of the Moon's surface were called
       <i>
        maria
       </i>
       (singular
       <i>
        mare
       </i>
       ) or seas, and the light parts were called
       <i>
        terrae
       </i>
       or continents.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Harriot" title="Thomas Harriot">
        Thomas Harriot
       </a>
       , as well as Galilei, drew the first telescopic representation of the Moon and observed it for several years. His drawings, however, remained unpublished.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOO_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-MOO-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first map of the Moon was made by the Belgian cosmographer and astronomer
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_Florent_van_Langren" title="Michael Florent van Langren">
        Michael Florent van Langren
       </a>
       in 1645.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOO_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-MOO-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Two years later a much more influential effort was published by
       <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Hevelius" title="Johannes Hevelius">
        Johannes Hevelius
       </a>
       . In 1647 Hevelius published
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Selenographia" title="Selenographia">
         Selenographia
        </a>
       </i>
       , the first treatise entirely devoted to the Moon. Hevelius's nomenclature, although used in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">
        Protestant
       </a>
       countries until the eighteenth century, was replaced by the system published in 1651 by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">
        Jesuit
       </a>
       astronomer
       <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Riccioli" title="Giovanni Battista Riccioli">
        Giovanni Battista Riccioli
       </a>
       , who gave the large naked-eye spots the names of seas and the telescopic spots (now called craters) the name of philosophers and astronomers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOO_7-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-MOO-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1753 the Croatian Jesuit and astronomer
       <a href="/wiki/Roger_Joseph_Boscovich" title="Roger Joseph Boscovich">
        Roger Joseph Boscovich
       </a>
       discovered the absence of atmosphere on the Moon. In 1824
       <a href="/wiki/Franz_von_Gruithuisen" title="Franz von Gruithuisen">
        Franz von Gruithuisen
       </a>
       explained the formation of craters as a result of
       <a href="/wiki/Meteorite" title="Meteorite">
        meteorite
       </a>
       strikes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The possibility that the Moon contains vegetation and is inhabited by selenites was seriously considered by major astronomers even into the first decades of the 19th century. In 1834–1836,
       <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Beer" title="Wilhelm Beer">
        Wilhelm Beer
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Johann_Heinrich_M%C3%A4dler" title="Johann Heinrich Mädler">
        Johann Heinrich Mädler
       </a>
       published their four-volume
       <i>
        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
         <i>
          Mappa Selenographica
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       and the book
       <i>
        <span lang="de" xml:lang="de">
         <i>
          Der Mond
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       in 1837, which firmly established the conclusion that the Moon has no bodies of water nor any appreciable atmosphere.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Space_race">
        Space race
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploration_of_the_Moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Space race">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">
        Space Race
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Moon_landing" title="Moon landing">
        Moon landing
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_manned_lunar_programs" title="Soviet manned lunar programs">
        Soviet manned lunar programs
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">
        Cold War
       </a>
       -inspired "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_race" title="Space race">
        space race
       </a>
       " and "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moon_race" title="Moon race">
        Moon race
       </a>
       " between the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States of America
       </a>
       accelerated with a focus on the Moon. This included many scientifically important firsts, such as the first photographs of the then-unseen
       <a href="/wiki/Far_side_of_the_Moon" title="Far side of the Moon">
        far side of the Moon
       </a>
       in 1959 by the Soviet Union, and culminated with the landing of the first humans on the Moon in 1969, widely seen around the world as one of the pivotal events of the 20th century, and indeed of human history in general.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luna_3_moon.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="384" data-file-width="500" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Luna_3_moon.jpg/220px-Luna_3_moon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Luna_3_moon.jpg/330px-Luna_3_moon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Luna_3_moon.jpg/440px-Luna_3_moon.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Luna_3_moon.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The first image returned of another world from space showed the Moon's far side.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2355" data-file-width="2340" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg/200px-Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg/300px-Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg/400px-Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moon-apollo17-schmitt_boulder.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_17" title="Apollo 17">
          Apollo 17
         </a>
         astronaut
         <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Schmitt" title="Harrison Schmitt">
          Harrison Schmitt
         </a>
         standing next to a boulder at Taurus-Littrow during the third EVA (extravehicular activity).
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
           NASA
          </a>
          photo.
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first man-made object to reach the Moon was the unmanned Soviet probe
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_2" title="Luna 2">
        Luna 2
       </a>
       , which made a hard landing on September 14, 1959, at 21:02:24 Z. The far side of the Moon was first photographed on October 7, 1959, by the Soviet probe
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_3" title="Luna 3">
        Luna 3
       </a>
       . Though vague by today's standards, the photos showed that the far side of the Moon almost completely lacked
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_mare" title="Lunar mare">
        maria
       </a>
       . In an effort to compete with these Soviet successes, U.S. President
       <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">
        John F. Kennedy
       </a>
       proposed the national goal of landing a human on the Moon. Speaking to a Joint Session of Congress on May 25, 1961, he said
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        "First, I believe that this nation should commit itself to achieving the goal, before this decade is out, of landing a man on the Moon and returning him safely to the earth. No single space project in this period will be more impressive to mankind, or more important for the long-range exploration of space."
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
         <a href="#cite_note-9">
          [9]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       The Soviets nonetheless remained in the lead for some time.
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_9" title="Luna 9">
        Luna 9
       </a>
       was the first probe to soft land on the Moon and transmit pictures from the lunar surface on February 3, 1966. It was proven that a lunar lander would not sink into a thick layer of dust, as had been feared. The first artificial satellite of the Moon was the Soviet probe
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_10" title="Luna 10">
        Luna 10
       </a>
       , launched March 31, 1966.
      </p>
      <p>
       On December 24, 1968, the crew of
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_8" title="Apollo 8">
        Apollo 8
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Frank_Borman" title="Frank Borman">
        Frank Borman
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jim_Lovell" title="Jim Lovell">
        James Lovell
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/William_Anders" title="William Anders">
        William Anders
       </a>
       , became the first human beings to enter lunar orbit and see the far side of the Moon in person. Humans first landed on the Moon on July 20, 1969. The first human to walk on the lunar surface was
       <a href="/wiki/Neil_Armstrong" title="Neil Armstrong">
        Neil Armstrong
       </a>
       , commander of the U.S. mission
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">
        Apollo 11
       </a>
       . The first robot
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_rover" title="Lunar rover">
        lunar rover
       </a>
       to land on the Moon was the Soviet vessel
       <a href="/wiki/Lunokhod_1" title="Lunokhod 1">
        Lunokhod 1
       </a>
       on November 17, 1970, as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Lunokhod_programme" title="Lunokhod programme">
        Lunokhod programme
       </a>
       . To date, the last human to stand on the Moon was
       <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Cernan" title="Eugene Cernan">
        Eugene Cernan
       </a>
       , who as part of the mission
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_17" title="Apollo 17">
        Apollo 17
       </a>
       , walked on the Moon in December 1972.
       <i>
        See also:
       </i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_lunar_astronauts" title="List of lunar astronauts">
        A full list of lunar Apollo astronauts
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Moon_rock" title="Moon rock">
        Moon rock samples
       </a>
       were brought back to Earth by three Luna missions (
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_16" title="Luna 16">
        Luna 16
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_20" title="Luna 20">
        20
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_24" title="Luna 24">
        24
       </a>
       ) and the Apollo missions 11 through 17 (except
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_13" title="Apollo 13">
        Apollo 13
       </a>
       , which aborted its planned lunar landing).
      </p>
      <p>
       From the mid-1960s to the mid-1970s there were 65 Moon landings (with 10 in 1971 alone), but after
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_24" title="Luna 24">
        Luna 24
       </a>
       in 1976 they suddenly stopped. The Soviet Union started focusing on
       <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">
        Venus
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">
        space stations
       </a>
       and the U.S. on
       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">
        Mars
       </a>
       and beyond, and on the
       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">
        Skylab
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">
        Space Shuttle
       </a>
       programs.
      </p>
      <p>
       Before the Moon race the US had pre-projects for scientific and military moonbases: the
       <a href="/wiki/Lunex_Project" title="Lunex Project">
        Lunex Project
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Project_Horizon" title="Project Horizon">
        Project Horizon
       </a>
       . Besides manned landings, the abandoned
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_manned_lunar_programs" title="Soviet manned lunar programs">
        Soviet manned lunar programs
       </a>
       included the building of a multipurpose moonbase "
       <a href="/wiki/Zvezda_(moonbase)" title="Zvezda (moonbase)">
        Zvezda
       </a>
       ", the first detailed project, complete with developed mockups of expedition vehicles
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and surface modules.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_exploration">
        Recent exploration
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploration_of_the_Moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Recent exploration">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1025" data-file-width="1084" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moon_seen_by_Cassini_-_PIA02321.tif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini–Huygens">
          Cassini–Huygens
         </a>
         took this image during its lunar flyby, before it traveled to
         <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">
          Saturn
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1990 Japan visited the Moon with the
       <a href="/wiki/Hiten" title="Hiten">
        Hiten
       </a>
       spacecraft, becoming the third country to place an object in orbit around the Moon. The spacecraft released the
       <a href="/wiki/Hiten" title="Hiten">
        Hagoromo
       </a>
       probe into lunar orbit, but the transmitter failed, thereby preventing further scientific use of the mission. In September 2007, Japan launched the
       <a href="/wiki/SELENE" title="SELENE">
        SELENE
       </a>
       spacecraft, with the objectives "to obtain scientific data of the lunar origin and evolution and to develop the technology for the future lunar exploration", according to the JAXA official website.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-index_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-index-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">
        European Space Agency
       </a>
       launched a small, low-cost lunar orbital probe called
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SMART_1" title="SMART 1">
        SMART 1
       </a>
       on September 27, 2003. SMART 1's primary goal was to take three-dimensional
       <a href="/wiki/X-ray" title="X-ray">
        X-ray
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Thermography" title="Thermography">
        infrared imagery
       </a>
       of the lunar surface. SMART 1 entered lunar
       <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">
        orbit
       </a>
       on November 15, 2004 and continued to make observations until September 3, 2006, when it was intentionally crashed into the lunar surface in order to study the impact plume.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       China has begun the
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Lunar_Exploration_Program" title="Chinese Lunar Exploration Program">
        Chinese Lunar Exploration Program
       </a>
       for exploring the Moon and is investigating the prospect of lunar mining, specifically looking for the
       <a href="/wiki/Isotope" title="Isotope">
        isotope
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Helium-3" title="Helium-3">
        helium-3
       </a>
       for use as an energy source on Earth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       China launched the
       <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_1" title="Chang'e 1">
        Chang'e 1
       </a>
       robotic lunar
       <a href="/wiki/Orbiter" title="Orbiter">
        orbiter
       </a>
       on October 24, 2007. Originally planned for a one-year mission, the Chang'e 1 mission was very successful and ended up being extended for another four months. On March 1, 2009, Chang'e 1 was intentionally impacted on the lunar surface completing the 16-month mission. On October 1, 2010, China launched the
       <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_2" title="Chang'e 2">
        Chang'e 2
       </a>
       lunar orbiter. China landed the
       <a href="/wiki/Rover_(space_exploration)" title="Rover (space exploration)">
        rover
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_3" title="Chang'e 3">
        Chang'e 3
       </a>
       on the Moon on December 14, 2013, became the third country to have done so.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Chang'e 3 is the first spacecraft to soft-land on lunar surface since
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_24" title="Luna 24">
        Luna 24
       </a>
       in 1976.
      </p>
      <p>
       India's national space agency,
       <a href="/wiki/Indian_Space_Research_Organisation" title="Indian Space Research Organisation">
        Indian Space Research Organisation
       </a>
       (ISRO), launched
       <a href="/wiki/Chandrayaan-1" title="Chandrayaan-1">
        Chandrayaan-1
       </a>
       , an unmanned lunar orbiter, on October 22, 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The lunar probe was originally intended to orbit the Moon for two years, with scientific objectives to prepare a three-dimensional atlas of the near and far side of the Moon and to conduct a chemical and mineralogical mapping of the lunar surface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The unmanned
       <a href="/wiki/Moon_Impact_Probe" title="Moon Impact Probe">
        Moon Impact Probe
       </a>
       landed on the Moon at 15:04 GMT on November 14, 2008
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       making India the fourth country to touch down on the lunar surface. Among its many achievements was the discovery of the widespread presence of water molecules in lunar soil.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_Missile_Defense_Organization" title="Ballistic Missile Defense Organization">
        Ballistic Missile Defense Organization
       </a>
       and NASA launched the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clementine_mission" title="Clementine mission">
        Clementine mission
       </a>
       in 1994, and
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Prospector" title="Lunar Prospector">
        Lunar Prospector
       </a>
       in 1998. NASA launched the
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter">
        Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter
       </a>
       , on June 18, 2009, which has collected imagery of the Moon's surface. It also carried the Lunar Crater Observation and Sensing Satellite (
       <a href="/wiki/LCROSS" title="LCROSS">
        LCROSS
       </a>
       ), which investigated the possible existence of water in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cabeus" title="Cabeus">
        Cabeus crater
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Gravity_Recovery_and_Interior_Laboratory" title="Gravity Recovery and Interior Laboratory">
        GRAIL
       </a>
       is another mission, launched in 2011.
      </p>
      <p>
       The first commercial mission to the Moon was accomplished by the
       <a href="/wiki/Manfred_Memorial_Moon_Mission" title="Manfred Memorial Moon Mission">
        Manfred Memorial Moon Mission
       </a>
       (4M), led by
       <a href="/wiki/Luxspace" title="Luxspace">
        LuxSpace
       </a>
       , an affiliate of German
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OHB_System" title="OHB System">
        OHB AG
       </a>
       . The mission was carried on the Chinese Chang'e 5-T1 test spacecraft which was launched on 23 October 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The 4M spacecraft made a Moon flyby on a night of 28 October 2014, after which it entered elliptical Earth orbit, exceeding its designed lifetime by four times.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MoonLuxspace_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-MoonLuxspace-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plans">
        Plans
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Exploration_of_the_Moon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Plans">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_current_and_future_lunar_missions" title="List of current and future lunar missions">
        List of current and future lunar missions
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LRO_2006.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="732" data-file-width="1046" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/LRO_2006.jpg/220px-LRO_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/LRO_2006.jpg/330px-LRO_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/LRO_2006.jpg/440px-LRO_2006.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LRO_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
          NASA
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter">
          Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Following the abandoned US
       <a href="/wiki/Constellation_program" title="Constellation program">
        Constellation program
       </a>
       , plans for manned flights followed by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moonbase" title="Moonbase">
        moonbases
       </a>
       were declared by Russia, Europe (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESA" title="ESA">
        ESA
       </a>
       ), China, Japan and India. All of them intend to continue the exploration of Moon with more unmanned spacecraft.
      </p>
      <p>
       China planned to conduct a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sample_return_mission" title="Sample return mission">
        sample return mission
       </a>
       with its
       <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_5" title="Chang'e 5">
        Chang'e 5
       </a>
       spacecraft in 2017, but that mission has been postponed until 2019 due to the 2017 failure of the
       <a href="/wiki/Long_March_5" title="Long March 5">
        Long March 5
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Launch_vehicle" title="Launch vehicle">
        launch vehicle
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foust_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-foust-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It will also send
       <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_4" title="Chang'e 4">
        Chang'e 4
       </a>
       , the backup model of the
       <a href="/wiki/Chang%27e_3" title="Chang'e 3">
        Chang'e 3
       </a>
       lander) to the
       <a href="/wiki/Far_side_of_the_Moon" title="Far side of the Moon">
        lunar farside
       </a>
       in 2018.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since the Chang'e 3 mission was a success, the backup lander Chang'e 4 is re-purposed for the mission to the farside, which will be the first time it is attempted by any of the space faring countries.
      </p>
      <p>
       India expects to launch another lunar mission by 2018, the
       <a href="/wiki/Chandrayaan-2" title="Chandrayaan-2">
        Chandrayaan-2
       </a>
       , which would place a motorized
       <a href="/wiki/Rover_(space_exploration)" title="Rover (space exploration)">
        rover
       </a>
       on the Moon.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SciExaminer_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SciExaminer-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Japanese Aerospace Exploration Agency (
       <a href="/wiki/JAXA" title="JAXA">
        JAXA
       </a>
       ) plans a manned lunar landing around 2020 that would lead to a manned lunar base by 2030; however, there is no budget yet for this project and the plan reverts to robotic missions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Russia also announced to resume its previously frozen project
       <a href="/wiki/Luna-Glob" title="Luna-Glob">
        Luna-Glob
       </a>
       , an unmanned lander and orbiter, which is slated to launch in 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2015,
       <a href="/wiki/Roscosmos" title="Roscosmos">
        Roscosmos
       </a>
       stated that Russia plans to place an astronaut on the Moon by 2030 leaving Mars to NASA. The purpose is to work jointly with NASA and avoid a space race
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Germany also announced in March 2007 that it would launch a national lunar orbiter,
       <a href="/wiki/LEO_(spacecraft)" title="LEO (spacecraft)">
        LEO
       </a>
       in 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However the mission was cancelled due to budgetary constraints.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In August 2007, NASA stated that all future missions and explorations of the Moon will be done entirely using the
       <a href="/wiki/International_System_of_Units" title="International System of Units">
        metric system
       </a>
       . This was done to improve cooperation with space agencies of other countries which already use the metric system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The European Space Agency has also announced its intention to send a manned mission to the Moon, as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Aurora_programme" title="Aurora programme">
        Aurora programme
       </a>
       . In September 2010, the agency introduced a "Lunar lander" programme with a target of autonomous mission to the Moon in 2018.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On September 13, 2007, the
       <a href="/wiki/X_Prize_Foundation" title="X Prize Foundation">
        X Prize Foundation
       </a>
       , in concert with
       <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
        Google, Inc.
       </a>
       , announced the
       <a href="/wiki/Google_Lunar_X_Prize" title="Google Lunar X Prize">
        Google Lunar X Prize
       </a>
       . This contest requires competitors "to land a privately funded robotic rover on the Moon that is capable of completing several mission objectives, including roaming the lunar surface for at least 500 meters and sending video, images and data back to the Earth."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In March 2014,
       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">
        SpaceX
       </a>
       indicated that while their current focus is not on Lunar
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_transport" title="Space transport">
        space transport
       </a>
       , they will consider
       <a href="/wiki/Private_spaceflight" title="Private spaceflight">
        commercial
       </a>
       launch contracts for one-off Moon missions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tss20140321_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-tss20140321-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
